(E) Divide the restoration area, specifying which areas need to be restored urgently and which areas can be delayed, and then start with those who want to be restored first. It was resolved to be submitted to the executive committee for handling. (F) Urgently convene the main local requirements to build houses, and convene the silver and money industry to provide financial assistance. It was resolved to be submitted to the executive committee for handling.

Citizens' Association Asks for the Promotion of Rent Reduction and Exemption 162

Letters to the Municipal Party Department and Three Courts The Shanghai Citizens' Association yesterday submitted letters to the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, the Shanghai Special District First Local Court, the Shanghai Special District Second Local Court, and the Shanghai Local Court for rent reduction and exemption, requesting consideration of citizens with weak economic capacity. The following is a transcript of the submission:

Submission to the Municipal Party Department: Respectfully submitted, the citizens of Shanghai with weak economic capacity have already been facing difficulties since the world economic recession, the high price of gold and the cheap price of silver, and the floods in various provinces. The various painful states of the Japanese army coming to Shanghai to disturb the situation are like icing on the cake. The only thing that these citizens lack is weak economic capacity, but their hard work, dedication, and public-spiritedness are truly rare. They are always eager to donate money for disaster relief, comfort Ma Zhanshan, aid the 19th Route Army, and relieve the disaster-stricken people, even when they have no money to reduce and no means to save. The hope for rent reduction and exemption is originally to solve difficulties by themselves, and indirectly it is to seek the gradual restoration of the market. Renting out buildings for rent is also a legal matter to seek profit, but the unexpected benefits they get at ordinary times are really uncountable. The cost of digging fees, small rents, and opening doors is almost equal to the total cost of building the house, or even more. They use relocation to achieve the purpose of increasing the rent by 20% to 100%, which is even more commonplace. As for all the contributions they make to the society and the country, purchasing government bonds and treasury bills is avoided as much as possible, and donating money for disaster relief is limited to those who own little property and are enthusiastic about society and the country, such as Wang Xiaohui, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, etc. As for the anti-Japanese consolation money and patriotic donations, those who avoided going to Hong Kong existed, those who fled back to their original home existed, and there were iron doors as deep as the sea, with no way to ask. Most of the landlords in the special zone claimed to be foreign properties. Considering the situation and reasoning, from a fair point of view, the generations who only seek private interests, the administrative offices, and the judicial yamen rely on the provisions of the law and the needs of the facts. It is not too harsh to do their duties today. Moreover, what they lose is only a little of their past inappropriate profits and increasing their inexhaustible source of wealth. If we do not plan for it now, the citizens with weak economic capacity will either sit and wait for death, and all commercial bankruptcies will become unemployment, or they will organize small real estate companies that rent land and build houses day and night to raise prices and rents to each other, causing China's economic center and the world's commercial hub to lose its cohesion and become Chicago in the United States in succession. The method set by the Shanghai Municipal Government for the rent reduction and exemption problem can be justified for its difficulty in avoiding taboos and throwing stones at rats. However, based on the needs of the facts and the location of public interest, it seems that there is no need to worry and dare to do it. Why is it better for one family to cry than for the whole road to cry? Even if the demands of citizens with weak economic capacity are met, it will not lead to the tragedy of one family crying, but to prevent the tragedy of crying when they see the coffin. We have always known that your department takes the late Prime Minister's legacy of seeking the interests of the people as its duty. We respectfully ask you to use the power granted by law and promote the purpose of rent reduction and exemption based on the needs of the facts. The restoration of Shanghai's prosperity really depends on it.

Submission to the Three Courts: Also submitted to the Shanghai Special District First Local Court, the Shanghai Special District Second Local Court, and the Shanghai Local Court: Respectfully submitted, the port of Shanghai has suffered from the world economic recession, the sharp drop in silver prices, the floods in the Yangtze River area, and the recent disturbances by the Japanese army. The above effects, even if there is only one, citizens with weak economic capacity are directly or indirectly difficult to escape its oppression, let alone both. Since the end of the Shanghai chaos

After that, all the weak and small shops are trying to reduce wages, lay off personnel, cut expenses and save food. Everything can be done freely. That is, the owed customer accounts are either reduced interest or extended. There is also a lot of room for negotiation. Those who live on wages have also had their incomes greatly reduced or even no income due to wage cuts and layoffs. Their lives are empty of savings and they live on borrowing and pawn. Only for the rent is there no room for negotiation. Because the landlord's means of increasing profits such as rent increases and relocation during the prosperous period of commerce have never been automatic for rent reduction and exemption in the autumn of commercial depression. Occasionally, the requests are rarely reduced, and only 50% to 10% are reduced. It has never been doubled or increased by several layers like a rent increase. In addition, there are also digging fees, small rents, and opening fees during the lease. At ordinary times, the tenant can still barely cope with it. At this time, the tenant is exhausted. There are no regulations in the law that can be requested for rent reduction and exemption, and there are equal clauses that the landlord can request for rent increase. If there is, the judges can make judgments based on the facts and legal principles and based on their free will, so that the tenants with weak economic capacity can have the hope of getting out of the rut and not let the market plummet and both the landlords and tenants suffer. The association is most concerned about the reality of society. If the rent is not appropriately adjusted according to the law, the commercial function will be undermined first. Its disaster is really unimaginable. Therefore, we specially submit to your court to deal with the rent case with consideration and reason, so as to provide relief for public interests. Not only will the tenants be blessed, but the landlords will also have hope for the restoration of the market. Today's superficial losses can be used as a long-term plan for the future. I hope you will consider the situation. The citizens are very fortunate. The real interests of all Shanghai merchants and residents depend on it.

Telegram from the Anti-Opium Society Regarding Rumors of Opium Monopoly in Jiangsu, 163

Urging Gu Zhutong Not to Waver on the Wrong Path

The Chinese National Anti-Opium Society, due to the widespread rumors circulating recently about Jiangsu Province planning to implement an opium monopoly, sent a letter yesterday to Gu Zhutong, Chairman of Jiangsu Province, to inquire about the truth of the matter and offer earnest encouragement. Excerpts from the original letter are as follows: (Above omitted) Rumors have been rampant lately, all alleging that your province of Jiangsu is about to implement an opium monopoly, with Lu, the manager of Xinghua Bank, in negotiations to handle the procedures related to customs revenue sources and that realization is imminent. The Society was initially reluctant to believe this, given your distinguished service to the Party and the nation, which surely would preclude your intent to lead the people into ruin. After extensive inquiries, however, we cannot help but suspect the veracity of these rumors. While street gossip can be dismissed as unfounded, there is enough evidence to warrant further investigation. According to the Society's findings, opium seedlings stretch as far as the eye can see in the Huaiyang region of northern Jiangsu, and raw opium is abundant in Zhenjiang, Suzhou, Changzhou and other places. Notorious opium traffickers, opium addicts, and proponents of the monopoly have been scurrying between Zhenjiang and Shanghai, frequenting the doors of officials in Jiangsu Province. Mr. Xu's undertaking is not without cause. It is said that the previous mass resignation of the entire committee of your provincial government was also due to the failure to implement the monopoly plan. Our Society, entrusted by the people of the nation with the duty of combating drugs, is deeply disheartened by the Jiangsu provincial government's wavering on the path of drug prohibition. Opium is a scourge that will not only harm the Party and the nation, but also poison the people, a crime that can never be washed away. Chairman Gu, with your wisdom and superior intelligence, will certainly not be misled by flatterers and tarnish your good name for posterity. It is hoped that you will immediately straighten things out, eliminate the demonic influences, strictly enforce the prohibition of opium, and set an example for officials and the people. We earnestly hope that Chairman Gu will truly consider this and we await your clear instructions with great trepidation. Thus and so.

Four Important Cases in Shanghai's Shipping Industry 164

The Shanghai Shipping Association and the Pilots' Association held joint executive and supervisory committee meetings yesterday and resolved four important cases related to the shipping industry, which are of great significance and require urgent investigation and reporting as follows:

Recovering Pilotage Rights: Our country's pilotage rights have long been in the hands of foreigners. Last year, the Shanghai shipping industry petitioned the Ministry of Finance, the Ministry of Communications, and the Ministry of the Navy, requesting their recovery. However, the outbreak of war led to a de facto suspension of this effort. Yesterday, the executive and supervisory committees of the Pilots' Association held a meeting and noted that if pilotage rights had been recovered last year, the Japanese troops would not have been able to sneak into Liuhang during the January 28th Incident, and Japanese warships would not have been able to freely enter and exit the Huangpu River. From a national defense perspective, it is even more necessary to actively recover pilotage rights. Four measures for recovery were discussed and decided upon: (1) Request the Ministry of Communications to immediately recover all pilotage rights and terminate the contracts of foreign pilots. (2) If there are any vacancies or an increase in the number of pilots in the future, the Pilots' Association should use Chinese pilots as much as possible. (3) In the future, Chinese representatives should be included in any consultations on pilotage issues by the Pilots' Association. (4) The case of the five additional Chinese pilots promised by the customs authorities last year should be implemented immediately. This resolution will be submitted to the Ministry of Communications immediately for vigorous advocacy.

Establishing a Merchant School: The expenses of the Wusong Merchant Marine School were originally shared by various shipping merchants, with tonnage surcharges levied on all vessels to cover the school's costs. The personnel trained by the school were intended for use by Chinese ships. Now, the Shipping Association has decided that the school's expenses should be borne by the central government, and the surcharges levied on each vessel should be abolished. In the future, shipping merchants will raise their own funds to establish a merchant school, and the resulting maritime talent will be even more confidential.

Furthermore, the funding for the Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau should also be allocated by the central government, so that Shanghai shipping merchants are no longer burdened. A request will be submitted to the Ministry immediately.

Expediting the Issuance of Shipping Bonds: Ten million yuan in shipping bonds were approved by the central government long ago, but have not yet been issued. This year's war has resulted in losses for 43 Shanghai shipping companies, amounting to more than 4.7 million yuan. With the shipping industry now in decline, the central government is requested to issue the ten million yuan in bonds as soon as possible to provide subsidies and prevent bankruptcies.

Adding Passenger Manifests: After taking office, He Hanlan, the Director of the Shanghai Shipping Administration Bureau, sent a letter to all shipping companies, instructing them to add passenger manifests to all Jianghai vessels, as is done on foreign mail ships, to facilitate inspection. At the time, the Shipping Association held a meeting to discuss the matter. It was argued that Chinese ships operate mostly on short routes, and passengers are scattered, making it difficult to register them one by one. A request was made for exemption. Now, the Shipping Administration Bureau has sent two more letters urging compliance, ordering all shipping companies to add passenger manifests for first and second class passengers without fail. The Shipping Association has already instructed all shipping companies to comply.

In addition, there is a case regarding limiting the number of poor people allowed to board ships. It has been decided that the authorities should first crack down on this, and then the number of passengers allowed on each ship should be re-specified, it is said.

Local News 2

Reasons for the Extremely Hot Weather in Shanghai 165

The Yangtze River Area is Not Expected to Experience Floods This Year

A Discussion with Father Dragon of the Xujiahui Observatory

The recent hot weather in Shanghai, with temperatures reaching levels not seen in recent years, prompted the East China News Agency to visit Father Dragon, Director of the Xujiahui Catholic Church Observatory, yesterday. According to Father Dragon, the hot weather in Shanghai is due to tropical temperatures along Indochina and Annam, from where heat waves are continuously transported northeastward. This causes Shanghai to experience frequent hot southwest winds. In addition, there have been no typhoons lately, so the transportation of heat waves has not changed direction due to them, making Shanghai's climate increasingly hot. The absence of thunderstorms since the beginning of summer has made the evenings particularly hot. In the equatorial regions, however, there are large thunderstorms every day from 4:00 PM to 6:00 PM, so the nights are quite cool, in stark contrast to Shanghai's situation. Last year, the Yangtze River basin experienced an unprecedented flood due to excessive rainfall. This year, however, the Yangtze River basin has had very little rainfall, while North China, including Beiping and Shandong, has had fairly average rainfall. The situation is very good, and the Yangtze River basin is not expected to experience floods again this year, it is said.

Child Abducted During Evening Cool-Down 166

Qian Guanjin's Young Son Kidnapped

Thugs Threaten with Guns

Qian Guanjin, a 38-year-old local gardener, lives at No. 7, Lane 206, Rue Pére Robert, in the French Concession. He has two sons and three daughters. Last night, around 8:30 PM, the whole family was cooling off at the entrance of their home when four men approached. Two of them were wearing white shirts and pants, and two were wearing hats and riding bicycles. Upon arriving at the entrance, two of the men got off the bicycles and asked if Guanjin was home. Before Qian could answer, the thugs grabbed Qian's seven-year-old second son, named Miaofu, and carried him away. Seeing the situation, Qian cried out for help, but the thugs pulled out guns and threatened him. The thugs then loaded Miaofu onto a rickshaw and fled. One of the bicycles was left at the intersection of Avenue Albert. The number on the bicycle, 18749, was already blurred. Afterwards, the victim reported the incident to the French Concession Police, requesting an investigation.

Fortune Teller Arrested 167

The Murderer is Fan Hongsheng

The Police are Conducting a Strict Investigation

After the murder of female fortune teller Yang Wenying, fortune teller Cheng Meixian (age 48, from Hangzhou), who goes by the name "Diaoyuke," was suspected of involvement and was arrested by Chief Detective You A'gen and Su Changsheng of the Laoza Police Station in Room 225 of the New World Hotel. This morning, Cheng was brought before Judge Feng Shide of the First Special District Court for a preliminary hearing. The police lawyer, Ru Baoyi, stated the facts of the case, saying that in addition to Yang Wenying's murder, her mother, Wang Wushi, also sustained three knife wounds, two on her arms and one on her chest. According to the doctor, her injuries were not serious. The arrest of the defendant was based on Wang Wushi's testimony. The police investigation revealed that the actual murderer was someone else, but the suspect knew the deceased through the defendant's introduction. The police are currently conducting a strict investigation of the murderer and will soon bring him to justice. The court was asked to approve the defendant's detention for one week, and a photograph of Diaoyuke and the deceased together, as well as the witnesses' statements, were presented as evidence. Detective Su testified that after the incident, the deceased's family's servant came to report it. He then went to investigate and found the deceased dead in the courtyard inside the door, with her back to the sky. He then sent the deceased and Wang Wushi to Renji Hospital. Wang Wushi stated that the defendant was involved in the incident, so he first went to 4 Weixin Lane, Rue Mabile, to arrest him, but he was not there. He then went to the New World Hotel and arrested him, explaining the various relationships between the defendant and the deceased (details already reported in the newspaper and omitted here). Cheng Meixian testified that the deceased was sold into prostitution by her mother, Wang Wushi, when she was 13 years old. He redeemed her for 140 yuan and taught her fortune telling. He recently learned that Wenying had become addicted to opium, and he tried to dissuade her, but she pretended to comply and became even more addicted to opium. He really knew nothing about her murder, and Wang Wushi hates him because he did not supervise her strictly enough, causing her daughter to develop this addiction. Now she is falsely accusing him, he said. Judge Feng, after examining the testimony, ordered the defendant to be remanded in custody and scheduled another hearing in one week. The body of Yang Wenying, also known as Wang Wenying, was sent by the police to the autopsy room on Avenue Frelun. At around 10:00 AM, Inspector Zhan Liangce of the First Special District Court arrived to examine the body and ruled that the deceased, Wang Wenying, had indeed been stabbed to death with a knife, causing excessive bleeding. The defendant, Fan Hongsheng, is highly suspected of involvement and the police were instructed to conduct a strict investigation and bring him to court for questioning. Chen A'jin, the female servant, testified that a guest named Fan Hongsheng, wearing a suit, came on the day of the incident. She knew him before. He wanted to go to Lao Si's place with the young lady, but the young lady refused. The old lady was also in the room. While they were talking, Fan gave me two small coins and told me to buy cigarettes, but the coins were made of lead. When I returned, I saw that both the lady and the young lady had been stabbed and were bleeding profusely. Fan was gone, she said. Rickshaw driver Pan Changfu testified that he saw the old lady run out of the door, bleeding like beads, and then collapse. He then reported it to the local police, who chased the suspect. He saw a man in a suit running wildly in front, chasing him to Daqing Lane, where he lost sight of him. He then reported it to the police, it is said. Inspector Zhan, after examining the testimony, ruled that the deceased, Wang Wenying, had indeed been stabbed to death with a knife, causing excessive bleeding. The defendant, Fan Hongsheng, is highly suspected of involvement and the police were instructed to conduct a strict investigation and bring him to court for questioning. The lead coin was kept in the evidence vault, and the body was handed over to the Pushan Villa for coffining and burial.

The District Court Procuratorate to Become Independent Next Month 169

The Shanghai District Court Procuratorate was reorganized from the former Local Procuratorate. Its administrative scope was reduced and it was subordinated to the President of the Court. The Chief Prosecutor was responsible for the distribution of duties and services within the Procuratorate. Only in terms of financial matters did the President have no power. It is now said that the Ministry of Justice will make the Procuratorate independent again from August, as it was in the days of the Procuratorate.

Yichang Ship Captain Missing 170

The captain of the Yichang steamship of the American-owned Jiujiang Company suddenly went missing in Hankou. Yesterday, the company received a report that the captain was still missing. The search situation is reported as follows: The Yichang captain, Mr. Michelo J. Miclo, an American citizen, has been working for many years and is quite familiar with the Yangtze River. He left Shanghai for Chongqing on the 15th of this month and arrived in Hankou. At 3:10 PM, he was still on duty on the ship. At 3:30 PM, the ship had already left Hankou when the captain suddenly went missing. The crew searched everywhere but could not find him. They then reported it to the American gunboat on the Yangtze River for assistance. The American gunboat received the report and searched along the Yangtze River, both on land and water, but found no trace of him, nor was his body found. The deputy captain took over the Yichang, and before reaching Yichang, he prohibited all crew members, sailors, and passengers from leaving the ship, suspecting that someone on board had murdered the captain. When the crew and passengers disembarked, they were thoroughly searched and questioned one by one, but no suspicious person was found. The matter has become a mystery. After receiving the report, the Shanghai head office, considering the importance of navigation, sent a Westerner named Ao Yimeng as acting captain of the ship. They telegraphed the Hankou branch yesterday, ordering Mr. Wu to go to Yichang from Hankou to take over. They also notified Michelo's family and instructed all Jiang vessels to pay attention to the investigation. The Jiujiang Company had one cook and four passengers kidnapped by bandits in Chenlingji last month. Three people died and one went missing. The case is still unresolved. Unexpectedly, the strange incident of the captain's disappearance has now occurred.

Eighth Cholera Report from the Port Quarantine Office 171

Shanghai Cholera Mortality Rate Slightly Increased, Locally Produced Injectable Solution Most Effective, Guowenshe reports: Wu Liande, Director of the Port Quarantine Administration, issued the eighth cholera report yesterday, saying: (1) The weather has been unusually hot since the end of last week (July 16). The highest temperature on July 14 was 101.1 degrees (in the shade), the lowest was 75.6 degrees, and the average for the whole week was 87.8 degrees. However, the highest temperature under the sun reached 130 to 150 degrees. The highest humidity on July 11 was 95 degrees, the lowest humidity on July 12 was 48 degrees, and the average was 79.6 degrees. (2) The number of cholera cases seems to be slightly increasing this week, with a total of 318 cases and 16 deaths. The table is listed as follows:

District Cases Deaths Shanghai 83 4 Public Concession 141 (4 foreigners and overseas Chinese) 9 (1 foreigner and overseas Chinese) French Concession 46 0 Unknown Area 48 3 Total This Week 318 (4 foreigners and overseas Chinese) 16 (1 foreigner and overseas Chinese)

Total Previously 1337 (20 foreigners and overseas Chinese) 81 (7 foreigners and overseas Chinese) Total to the end of last week 1655 cases (24 foreigners and overseas Chinese) 98 deaths (8 foreigners and overseas Chinese) (3) The general public has a deep understanding of the benefits of cholera prevention injections, but there are still those who have not carefully used qualified injectable solutions. Often, products imported from Europe, America, and Japan are used. It should be known that using injectable solutions made from local strains is the most effective. For example, the injectable solutions produced by the Shanghai Public Concession Works Department and the Shanghai Municipal Health Laboratory are the best. There have been several cases of patients who still developed cholera after being injected with imported injectable solutions. (4) The benefits of early saline injection treatment (cholera initially causes sudden and rapid vomiting and diarrhea, which can excessively deplete the body's water, leading to general emaciation and cholera toxin poisoning, eventually leading to heart failure). Early treatment can neutralize toxins in the body, replenish water in the blood, and use saline to clear residual toxins from the intestines, thereby restoring heart function. There have been many cases of severely ill patients whose pulse lines were completely lost and turned bluish upon admission, who were able to talk and laugh freely after only half an hour of treatment. Therefore, the low mortality rate in Shanghai this time (6%) must be attributed to the early prevention efforts of the health authorities, especially the effectiveness of preventive injections and early medical treatment in hospitals for the majority of citizens. (5) The efficiency of cholera prevention and control in Shanghai is as described above, but it is regrettable that other cholera-epidemic provinces and regions in the country have not achieved the same efficiency. Cholera outbreaks have been found in Suzhou, Wuxi, Xiamen, Zhangzhou, Shantou, Suiyuan, Zhuozhou (between Beiping and Baoding), Nanchang (Jiangxi), and Baotou, with mortality rates of 4% to 50%. (6) Although the Japanese government has made great efforts to prevent and control cholera in Dalian, there have already been 20 cases, and there is deep concern about the spread of the epidemic to Liaoning, Jilin, Harbin, and the Northeast region. (7) According to the report from Director Wang of the Xiamen Port Quarantine Station, the newly built hospital has been able to accommodate a large number of cholera patients in the past two weeks. However, due to the narrowness of the hospital, straw sheds have been added to accommodate the large number of patients. The Xiamen Port Quarantine Hospital is the only hospital in the city that admits and treats cholera patients. (8) Many places have manufactured a large number of cholera prevention solutions, such as the Shanghai Municipal Health Laboratory, the Public Concession Works Department Chemical Laboratory, the Central Health Laboratory (Nanjing), the Central Epidemic Prevention Office (Beiping), the Northeast Epidemic Prevention Office (Harbin), and the South Manchuria Railway Health Laboratory (Dalian). The prices of these solutions are very low.

The Red Light at the Wusong Fort Lighthouse was Lit Yesterday 172

Installed to indicate the sea routes to the outside of the estuary. During the Sino-Japanese War, the signal light tower at the Wusong Fort, set up by the Jianghai Customs to guide ships, was destroyed by artillery shells, causing the red light at the top of the tower to go out. Afterwards, the Japanese army tried to repair the lighthouse and relit it. However, a red light on the pier in front of the flagpole room was also destroyed. This light is very important because it is used to indicate the sea routes outside the estuary. The Jianghai Customs engineer ordered craftsmen to repair it in Song and changed the light to use dry electricity (previously kerosene). The light flashes on and off, and there is no need for a lamplighter. It can automatically light up and shine day and night. It only needs to be recharged once every three months, which is very convenient. The installation has been completed, and it started burning yesterday.

Joint Meeting of the Fire Brigades in the Northern District of Shanghai 173

Discussing Ways to Cope with Financial Difficulties

The funds for the fire brigades in the northern districts of Shanghai have been collected from the local general donations by the municipal government and transferred to the Public Security Bureau for monthly allocation. Since the outbreak of the Shanghai War, the municipal treasury has been depleted, and each district has only received 60 yuan for maintenance. All the repair budgets and recurring expenses for the fire-fighting equipment damaged during the war, such as vehicles and leather belts, have been submitted and requested for allocation for relief repeatedly, but more than two months have passed without any news. A major fire occurred on Haichang Road a few days ago, burning more than 100 houses. The firefighters were unable to rescue the fire due to the lack of leather belts and the vehicles and important equipment were not yet repaired. If it were not for the neighboring and Nanshi Concession fire brigades to help extinguish the fire, the danger would have been unimaginable. The brigade and others now consider the local fire protection matters to be of great importance to the safety and security of the residents. No matter how difficult the municipal government's finances are, it should be given some consideration to maintain the safety of citizens' property and lives. It is said that a joint meeting will be convened at the First Section Fire Brigade at 5:00 PM today to discuss the problem of the delayed disbursement of fire protection funds in detail in order to find relief measures.

Continued Investigation of Relevant Persons in the Liu Nianchun Kidnapping Case 175

Liu Personally Came to Court to Testify

Describing the Kidnapping Process

Liu Nianchun, a native of Suzhou, is the manager of the Dingkang Gold Store on Tianjin Road. He lives at No. 922 North Chengdu Road. On the afternoon of July 5th of the previous year, at around 6:00 PM, he and his wife, Ms. Ma, were in their own car in front of their house, going somewhere, when he was kidnapped by bandits. His wife managed to pay a ransom of 20,000 yuan. On August 13th of that year, the Xinzha Police Station arrested the leader of the kidnappers, Yu Baocheng, and sent him to court for questioning. He was sentenced to death and has already been executed. On the 5th of this month, Sun Shaokun, a Chinese detective of the Jiaxing Road Police Station, learned that two drivers, Shao A'gen, who worked as drivers at the Lili Car Shop at No. 17 Suzhou Road, were involved in the case. He then coordinated with Western detectives to secretly go to their home (No. 325, Oujia Road) to arrest him and sent him to the First Special District Court for questioning. Yesterday, Judge Shen Bingrong held a continued hearing in the Fourth Criminal Court, and police lawyer Zhang Tianyin stated that the victim Liu Nianchun had come to court today and requested to ask questions, adding that the investigation revealed that the defendant was working as a driver for a lawyer surnamed Zhang at the time, and fled to Dalian after the incident, it is said. Then, according to Liu Nianchun's testimony, he and his wife had just boarded their own car parked at the entrance of the alley, and before the car door was closed, four bandits suddenly rushed into the car. Two bandits sat in front, scaring the driver Lu Lanfu into silence. The other two bandits sat next to him and drove quickly to Hongzhen, where they drove his wife and driver out of the car and the bandits who sat in the front were not able to be seen clearly. The two bandits who were guarding him had Jiangbei accents. The car went to a place, and the four bandits got out one after another. There were several other bandits who kidnapped him to a remote field and made him walk around. He was dizzy and exhausted. Later, he was taken to a small room with no windows, only a hole in the roof for light. Three bandits guarded him. Every night at 8:00 or 9:00 PM, two bandits came, wearing foreign hats that hung down and black glasses on their noses, about thirty years old, speaking the local dialect of Ningbo, and repeatedly threatened him. He ignored them. The three bandits who were guarding him looked like Shanghai locals. His wife paid 20,000 yuan to release him. He lived in the house for nine days, and the defendant was arrested. He was not one of the two who were sitting next to him in the car at the time. But he did not know whether the driver was there and could not specify. After this unfortunate incident, he cancelled the car, so the driver Lu had already resigned and he did not know where he was now. He did not think he had left Shanghai. If he knew, he might be willing to come to court to testify, he said. The defendant insisted that he did not know anything about Liu's kidnapping. He was working for a lawyer surnamed Zhang for about two weeks, and then resigned because the car was transferred. Later, he received a letter from his father in Dalian about a gramophone and went to Dalian on August 12th, staying for about three months. The court asked if the previous arrested criminal said that he went with him to rob land, and he answered no, and said that if it was confirmed that he was one of the kidnappers in Liu's case, he would be willing to be shot. Judge Shen, after examining the testimony, ordered him to be remanded in custody and scheduled another hearing.

The Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council is Recruiting Trainees 177

For the purpose of hiring Chinese inspectors, the Public Works Department of the Shanghai Municipal Council recruited eight Chinese trainees last year, with excellent results. It is now planning to recruit three more. Applicants must be between 21 and 23 years old, physically strong, able to speak the Shanghai dialect and Mandarin, and have a certificate from the Public Works Department's public schools or St. Francis Xavier's College, or a degree from another well-known university. If selected, they must train for six and a half years, but the period may be shortened depending on the trainee's talent and effort. After completing the training, they can be appointed as junior inspectors. After serving for another three years, they can be promoted to inspectors. The salary in the first year of probation is 75 yuan per month. After passing the probation, they will be formally enrolled as trainees, with a monthly salary of 100 yuan. If they pass the annual examination and continue to be employed, their monthly salary will be increased by 25 yuan. When promoted to junior inspector, the initial monthly salary is 250 yuan. When promoted to inspector, the monthly salary will be in accordance with the regulations of the bureau. Those who wish to apply for this traineeship can obtain an application form from Room 130A, 1st Floor, Health Department, No. 16 Hankou Road, fill it in personally, and submit it together with a photo and supporting documents to the department by registered mail or in person before August 1 for selection. Those who are selected must pay a cash deposit of 500 taels or have a guarantor recognized by the bureau. After being admitted, they must not engage in other businesses. Applicants must not seek interviews or canvass for support, otherwise they will be rejected. The results of those who are not selected will also be recorded for future reference or possible replacement, it is said.

Theft Case on Jun Gong Road Solved 183

Huang Guansheng Robbed of a Large Sum

Police Officers Immediately Solve the Case

Yesterday (20th) morning, around 3:20 AM, at No. 14 Sunjia Bridge, Jun Gong Road, north of Shanghai, the home of Huang Guansheng, a local bailiff, was suddenly visited by eight robbers. Two of the robbers, each holding real and fake pistols, immediately intimidated the victims and ordered them to remain silent and monitored their movements. Four robbers entered the house and searched for more than one hundred pieces of new silk and leather clothing, two gold rings, one gold bracelet, and one gold ear pick, worth more than 1,000 yuan. They packed the items into four bundles and carried them away. The victim immediately reported the incident to the Fifth District, Fourth Precinct (i.e., Yinxianggang Town), which notified all police stations to investigate. The Precinct Chief Liao Cheng-zhang and officer Wu Lin-zhi immediately led the police to the victim's home to investigate the scene.

For a week, they were split up and assigned to rigorously investigate in the countryside. The officers from the Jiangjiaxing Precinct Zhao Zhibin and Hu Wanshun were conducting routine patrol on the road when they spotted two suspects in the act of carrying large bundles. They were stopped to inquire the contents of the bundles. They blankly stared and could not answer. They only claimed that a friend from Wusong entrusted me to carry it to Caojiadu in western Shanghai. They were immediately taken to the precinct for interrogation. They were identified as accomplices in the robbery of Huang Guansheng's home. One of them was identified as Xia Jinlong and the other Yan Chengquan. The two were taken back to the Fourth Precinct along with the loot. Under close interrogation by Chief Liao, it was revealed that the rest of the loot was taken to Caojiadu by accomplices to divide the spoils. The firearms were located at Xia Jinquan's residence. Chief Liao immediately dispatched patrol officer He Shaoxiang and others who rushed through the night

went to Caojiadu and together with two police officers from the Sixth Precinct patrol for the arrest. On an open space in that location, the patrol located 5 or 6 thieves sitting on the ground and dividing the spoils. The patrolmen immediately rushed forward and arrested the thieves. The patrol immediately arrested Wang Aqhi and Li Qianlou. The remaining suspects managed to escape. Within those who escaped, the suspect Li was captured by the patrolman Wu Aile for being red-shirted without a waist belt. The arrest happened to be near a river which suspect jumped into for escape. Patrolman Wu Aile and Wang Keyi followed the chase. They gave chase and jumped into the river. The suspect was captured four times. The two patrolmen were tenacious and finally subdued the suspect. The two patrolmen fired over ten shots at the sky. Patrolman Wu's legs were severely wounded from jumping into the river. The loot were brought back to the Fourth Precinct for questioning. It was found that there was more loot hidden at a residence of a certain person on Carter Road (卡德路). The patrol were dispatched along with detectives to haul the loot from the residence. It was found that after inspection from Huang Guansheng that 200 yuan worth of goods was missing. Chief Liao Cheng-zhang stated that the case was solved in less than an hour. The patrol and officers made a valiant pursuit and patrolman Wu was injured. He immediately awarded the patrolmen 20 yuan for their efforts. The case along with the suspects and loot were submitted to the City Police Department for inquiry.

Letter to the Editor 195

To the Editor: I recently read a news item in the second column of your newspaper's local news section, entitled "(Dying at Home Instead of in Prison)," which stated that inmate Chen Changsheng was due to be released on the 17th of this month upon payment of the fine by his family. It was hoped that he would be released on that day, but it was not until yesterday (the 19th) that the release order was received from the province. The tone of the article suggests that this prison detained the prisoner for two extra days, which is not in accordance with the facts. After checking, inmate Chen Changsheng, who has been released, was sentenced by the Second Special District Court for opium-related crimes to one month of imprisonment and a fine of

30 yuan. He was sent to prison on June 28th of this year. After carefully examining the execution order sent to the prison by the court, it was noted that the starting date of his sentence was June 25th, with six days deducted, and the term expired on July 18th. After the expiration of the term, he was sent to the court for execution of the fine. According to Article 22 of Chapter 3 of the Criminal Law, this prison sent him to the court on July 19th in the forenoon in accordance with the law. This prison has records to prove it. Therefore, I am writing to request that your newspaper publish the original letter in the newspaper to clarify the truth. Sincerely, Shanghai Second Special District Prison, Jiangsu, July 20th.

On the 17th of this month, the Pacific Shipping Company's poor operations and the merging of the Taizi and Baohe ships, as reported in your newspaper's local news section, are not true. The Taizi ships are actually merged into E-Tai Company. The reason for the merger is not due to the poor operation of the Taizi ships. The Taizi ships will continue to operate to Shanghai and the ports of New York and Manila, alternating with E-Tai's Snow ships. Therefore, both shipping companies are merged and managed by E-Tai. It has nothing to do with Baohe. We hereby inform you and hope for a correction. E-Tai Shipping Company, July 21.

Incoming Correspondence

From Taels and Yuan to Silver and Paper 196

During times of great national turmoil, especially after the devastating January 28th Incident, the domestic industry has been in extreme decline. Farmers' economies are on the verge of bankruptcy. The essence of the country is concentrated in cities, which rely on the clothing and food necessary for life.

The people exhausted their possessions to trade for imported cloth and rice. Thus, the silver dollars and banknotes that once penetrated the interior flowed into the cities within half a year. To cope with import trade, there was a need for real silver, leading to a drastic drop in the ocean tael price to around 68 cents, an unprecedented situation. Under these extraordinary circumstances, the old idea of abolishing taels and adopting yuan has been revived. It is hoped that eloquent articles and great arguments will appear in newspapers, advocating that the time is ripe and it is a pity to miss it. More radical proponents are impatiently urging its completion, demanding the government swiftly enact it with a decree, believing that the currency system can be unified once silver taels are abolished. Those who oppose it argue that attempting such a fundamental change during a time of post-war chaos and abnormal finance may have other motives. They suspect the intention is to promote the issuance of paper money after the abolition of real silver taels, and even claim that the plummeting ocean tael price is not due to the overabundance of silver dollars but the abundance of paper money. According to actual surveys, the currency concentrated in Shanghai consists of no more than two or three parts silver dollars and seven or eight parts paper money. Furthermore, they criticize the previous government for recklessly permitting numerous official and private banks to have the right to issue banknotes. Over the past twenty years, the people have suffered from paper money, such as the Jitie banknotes in the three northeastern provinces, and the non-convertible banknotes of banks in Zhili, Henan, Shanxi, Shandong, and the Northwest provinces. The discounts on Chuan Taels and Hankou notes in Tianjin are recent lessons. They suspect whether the reserves of various issuing banks are genuine and comply with the law, as the government does not supervise and society does not care, allowing them to operate freely without restrictions, hiding dangers and creating risks. If an outbreak occurs, it will inevitably spread throughout the country. In this period, suddenly advocating the abolition of taels and the adoption of yuan is like adding fuel to the fire and pushing the boat in dangerous direction. European countries have complete currency systems, with both standard

and auxiliary currencies, and the right to issue money is controlled by the government. However, people still cannot avoid the disasters of paper money, such as the Russian ruble and the German mark, as everyone knows. Even recently, when Britain announced the suspension of convertibility and Japan banned the export of gold, prices plummeted. Isn't this all because countries over-issued paper money? Our country's currency system is complex and chaotic, the financial system is disorganized, and the issuance is not unified. If we rashly abolish taels and adopt yuan, it may cause widespread repercussions and inevitably trigger other disturbances, leading to social unrest. His words are like this, but I believe that abolishing taels and adopting yuan is only a partial issue in currency system reform, and it is not a purely political issue. It is indeed related to social economy, market conditions, and finance. The government must be able to carefully assess the timing, coordinate overall, and consider carefully. Silver taels are certainly on the list of things that must be abolished, and not suspended due to the opposition of a few. Regarding the disorganized issuance, proper plans must be made to learn from the past and prevent future troubles. Then, after silver taels are abolished, the financial system will be stable and the country and people will truly benefit from it.

Feng Bingnan Questions Ma Yinchu on the Issue of Abolishing Taels and Adopting Yuan 197

Recently, due to the sharp drop in the price of the ocean tael, the idea of abolishing taels and adopting yuan has arisen at the right time. The government is in favor of it, scholars are advocating it, and those in the financial community are also providing detailed analysis and expressing their views. This issue has become the center of public opinion. Although there are those who hold opposing views, they mostly express agreement with the principle of abolishing taels and adopting yuan. Those who are concerned and believe that caution is needed only differ on the steps to be taken. In my humble opinion, although the advocacy of abolishing taels and adopting yuan seems to be gradually converging, it would be too assertive to say that the principle can be debated without any argument. There are many examples in the world where something has been advocated by hundreds or thousands of people for a long time, but once it is implemented, it is constrained by the situation, and its drawbacks are immediately apparent before its benefits are seen. How many of the reforms in our country in the past have achieved the expected results? Often, the opposite is true. The use of taels has a long history, and what is old has become a habit, which cannot be changed suddenly. After the introduction of silver dollars, because they were named after foreigners, they were not a system owned by the country. Since taels can be merged into yuan, why can't yuan be abolished and taels retained? The effects are similar. Therefore, there is room for research on which of the two to choose. However, this is beyond the scope of this article and will be omitted for now. What I want to discuss here is Mr. Ma Yinchu's recent article on abolishing taels and adopting yuan. Mr. Ma speaks painfully about the chaos of our country's currency system, and especially believes that the diverse composition of silver taels and the local division are obstacles to the unification of the national currency. Therefore, he wants to catch the king and destroy the yuan to realize his silver dollar standard. His momentum is strong and his words are harsh. However, he also says that there are many types of silver dollars in our country, and the composition varies in quality. He is also dissatisfied with silver dollars like we are. The only difference is that Mr. Ma believes that since the market price of the ocean tael has repeatedly fallen, silver dollars with higher quality have been melted down, and those that have not been melted down are mostly inferior silver dollars. The composition may be unified, which is of great benefit to the unification of the silver dollar composition. Therefore, he believes that it is a good opportunity to abolish taels and adopt yuan. He also says that "(The money shops say that abolishing taels and adopting yuan must be done after the unification of hard and soft currencies. This is really illogical. Who can draw this conclusion on what comes first and what comes later? It seems too boring for the money shops to say this. The purpose of abolishing silver and using yuan today is to unify hard currency. There is absolutely no reason why hard currency can be unified without abolishing silver taels.)" However, we believe that since we want to abolish taels, the shortcomings of taels seem to be of no use to attack, and the harms of yuan cannot but be eliminated first. Otherwise, although taels are abolished, the harm to the people will be more severe than when taels and yuan are used together. Let's set an example to clarify this. Suppose there are two parties, A and B, who share the power of government. They are constantly fighting for the country, and the people are suffering. Once the people want to overthrow Party A to support Party B to take sole power, hoping to benefit the country, then the minimum requirement must be to first check whether Party B's policies are necessary for the times, and whether the words and deeds of its members are trusted by the people. Only after a satisfactory check can they be entrusted with major policies, hoping that the subsequent effects will not be that Party A's policies are bad and its members are not popular, and then strongly claim that Party B's policies must be good and its members must be good, and once they take sole power, they will definitely benefit the country and the people. This analogy cannot be said to be illogical. The fact that the composition of silver dollars today is uneven and that paper money floods the market has been recognized. If we do not start by reorganizing hard currencies, but rashly abolish taels and adopt yuan, then those who independently mint coins in various provinces will be the same, and those who issue paper money from various banks will be the same. Taels will be abolished, but the currency system will still be the same. After a disturbance, there must be people who take the opportunity to profit, and the result will still be suffered by the general majority of the people. There is no doubt about this. Although the Shanghai Mint can mint 500,000 new coins a day, what good does it do to the unification of the currency system? This is why we are hesitant to agree with the idea of rashly changing the yuan without first reorganizing soft and hard currencies. Also, Mr. Ma says that paper money will not be over-issued after the yuan is changed. We cannot help but doubt it. Since it is said that it will not be over-issued, then it must be issued. If it is necessary to issue, then who can guarantee that it will not be abused? Mr. Ma says that there are 220 million silver taels and 50 million taels in Shanghai. Assuming that this number is accurate, then after the abolition of taels, Shanghai alone will need to increase paper money by 70 million yuan. In addition to the number that should be issued after the abolition of silver taels nationwide, the number must be alarming. How can it be said that it is not much? May I ask, if the soft currency has not been reorganized and the right to issue has not been unified, and then this huge amount is added out of nowhere, what will be the impact on society and people's livelihood? How can we not think deeply about it? Mr. Ma's article lists three reasons for those who oppose the abolition of taels and the adoption of yuan. Except for the first one, that the government profits from it, we do not want to treat others with a distrustful heart and will not say a word. As for the other two, as discussed above, Mr. Ma says that they seem right but are actually wrong, but we believe that they seem wrong but are actually right. I dare to use the meaning of "Everyone speaks their mind" and briefly express my thoughts. I sincerely hope that people of the country will express their views and judge them so that the truth can be clarified.

After Mr. Ma's article lists all the good things that banks will have after the abolition of taels and the adoption of yuan, and the psychology of the money shops' opposition, it is thorough and should have everything. Mr. Ma may have written it in a moment of excitement, with no intention of being reasonable. However, the words are close to defamation and involve trivial matters. Rebutting this would turn against the main point, so I will not repeat it.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Speech

Gu Weijun's Talk in Jinan 198

-- Fo

Mr. Gu Weijun spoke to reporters at Jinan Railway Station on the 18th. The most important meanings in his conversation were these two sentences:

"Foreign affairs and military affairs depend on the government to preside over, and the people should assist. Recently, Japanese goods have increased,

how will the people of our country explain themselves?"

These two sentences are completely correct, but I still want to make it clear that since the September 18th and January 28th incidents, the severe oppression and destruction of the Japanese army against the Chinese people has been unprecedented in the history of our country. Now, for the Chinese to go to sell Japanese goods is truly living in a drunken dream, losing all conscience. However, this matter cannot be blamed on the general public. The worst are a few greedy merchants, while the general public is only seeking petty profits and lacks the ability to distinguish. The lack of progress of our country's people is originally unexplainable. However, the government cannot shirk its responsibility. Why has the anti-Japanese movement in Shanghai suddenly become silent?

If foreign affairs and military affairs must rely on the government to preside over, this is of course the case. If not the government, who else can we rely on? However, whether the government can be relied upon or not is a question. Since the September 18th Incident, slogans such as long-term resistance to recover lost territory have long been heard. However, how to recover and how to resist are still hovering in our minds and have not been dreamed of yet. Now, the Japanese army is trying to advance into Rehe, bombing Chaoyang City. The situation is very dangerous. Military officers who have always advocated non-resistance are naturally incurable. However, what should military officers who claim long-term resistance and the recovery of lost territory do?

As for the people's assistance, there is no need to worry about it. Just look at the people's assistance to the brave resistance against the Japanese at Zhamashan, and the people's assistance to the brave resistance against the Japanese by the 19th Route Army. This kind of assistance comes entirely from the people's initiative. From this point of view, how eager are the people's patriotic concepts? If the government can send troops to recover lost territory, the people's assistance will definitely be even more enthusiastic. Now, it is not that the people are not helping, but that they are powerless to help.

As for the mainland people's dissatisfaction with the central government, it is mostly due to this. If the central government once mobilized a large army and attacked directly, no matter whether it is the reactionary army or the Communist army, if there are any who take the opportunity to cause chaos and try to destroy it, our people should unanimously

rise up and abandon them together!

Science

Artificial Marble 201

— Luo Xiqin

Marble is widely used in architecture and crafts, its value comparable to that of a city. However, its production is limited by geographical and other factors, unlike granite, which can be easily extracted anywhere without fear of depletion.

Let's not discuss foreign countries for the moment. Within China, the areas rich in marble are limited to Dali in Yunnan and Qiyang in Hunan. However, both are located deep inland, making it difficult to continuously supply the needs of large coastal commercial and industrial cities. In this respect, promoting the modernization of our lives faces a dilemma in its path of development: one is to strive for scientific production, and the other is to beg for the surplus of friendly nations with huge sums of money.

Artificial marble is a kind of successful experiment in which we use scientific methods to make something similar to natural marble. If you have the right tools and fine techniques, and follow the sequence below, the results will often bring well-deserved comfort to the brave men and women dedicated to the craft.

(1) Materials (A) Pure white cement is sold in Shanghai, mostly imported, and more than twice as expensive as ordinary cement used for reinforced concrete. In fact, there is little difference between the method of making this cement and ordinary cement, but pure limestone (such as calcite) and pure aluminum silicate (such as kaolin) must be selected as raw materials. When mixing and pulverizing them, avoid direct friction with ironware (replace with hard stone or pottery) to prevent iron filings from mixing in and destroying its whiteness. (B) Crystalline quartz fragments with edges, screened through two sieves with different mesh sizes, and the middle layer of uniform volume is taken for use. (C) Finely ground metal oxide pigments, dissolved in water, and organic pigments that fade over time are not suitable.

Same hot weather, different ways to cool off. Lushan bean sheds, each with its own charm. Buddhist inscription

For pink, take one part of ammonium-precipitated stannic chloride, one part of zinc oxide, and one part of aluminum oxide, mix evenly and calcine in a refractory clay crucible.

For sky blue, calcine 0.05 parts of cobalt oxide, 2 parts of aluminum oxide, and 1.5 parts of zinc oxide.

For emerald green, grind evenly 0.05 parts of chromium oxide, 2 parts of zinc oxide, and 2 parts of calcined borax, put them into a crucible, and wash and grind them finely after calcination. Note: The above three pigments, with low-temperature coal flux, are suitable for painting on ceramics and glass.

(2) Tools (A) Shallow pans made of galvanized iron sheet, welded according to the size and shape of tabletops and screens. (B) Plaster of Paris, lithographic stone, etc. are used to cast negative molds of statues and other sculptures, i.e., seed molds. (C) Lithographic stone, rosin, tallow, turpentine. (D) Large wooden buckets for mixing cement and earthenware bowls for mixing pigments, iron pots for melting wax, stirring rods. (E) Jing Mountain stone powder for polishing (this powder is used for polishing jade and glass), foot-operated grinding wheel.

(3) Processing: First, let's describe the construction of artificial flat marble slabs. Take the above-made galvanized iron shallow pan, coat it with a lubricant made of molten wax, rosin, and tallow in an iron pot until dry, and place it on a platform. Then, take seven parts of the weighed white cement and three parts of crystalline quartz sand, mix them with water in a wooden bucket to form a paste, pour it into the pan, shake it flat and let it dry. After it hardens, use hot water to heat the bottom surface of the lead pan, the wax will melt, and it will easily fall off. Use Jing Mountain stone powder and water to hone it on a smooth and flat whetstone, and you will get a crystal-clear and white flat

marble slab.

If you want red veins, you should mix a bowl of pink cement slurry separately when mixing the cement (add the above-mentioned pink pigment), pour it into a large wooden bucket, and skillfully mix it into a pattern like veins and flowers, pour it into a galvanized iron pan and let it dry. The procedure for blue veins is the same, only the pigment is changed.

If you want emerald green landscape patterns, you can also rely on the skill of splashing ink to form a dragon, and reap the rewards of your own efforts. Regarding the surgery of making statue molds, I will discuss it in detail when I discuss wax figures and plaster crafts in another section. However, casting statues of artificial marble is also based on the above-mentioned method of preparing flat marble.

I have nothing more to say.

### False Alarm 202

— Former Master of Zhenglou

I have a friend named Jin, who is studying Chinese with Mr. Hu Huaichen in Jing County, he is a very honest young man. His father runs a shop in the western part of this city. After he graduated from middle school, his father would not allow him to continue his studies, and asked him to help with the shop business... But he loves literature and is eager to learn. Although he did not step into a towering university to continue his studies, he finally joined the Chinese language tutoring class set up by Mr. Hu. In addition, he is also studying at a night school. He stayed at his friend's house in Shanghai at night.

He usually likes to read books and magazines published in the market. Regardless of whether they are new or old, good or bad, he always buys new publications to read. Therefore, this false alarm was also a punishment for indiscriminately reading magazines without discernment! Because he recently saw a literary magazine, which contained a message that a certain literary society on Ximen Road was recruiting members. This touched his love of literature, so yesterday morning (the 19th), he came out of his friend's house where he was staying, and rode his own bicycle straight to the so-called literary society on Ximen Road to ask for a copy of the charter to read.

When he arrived inside, there was a person guarding it, who said to him: "Wait upstairs! I'll go get the charter." He was waiting upstairs, and in a moment, many Chinese and Western detectives came and surrounded him. The first Chinese detective asked him, "Aren't you here to die? Why do you want to join the Communist Party?" At this time, he was really like a monk of丈二, unable to figure out what was going on. It turned out that the so-called literary society was an organ of the Communist Party, which had been cracked down on the day before yesterday. At this time, the police were waiting for accomplices. Seeing him coming so early to ask for the charter, they suspected that he was a red element. Therefore, without allowing him to explain, they caught him and took him to the Songshan Road Police Station. They took out many photos and asked him, "Do you know these people?" He said, "I'm here to ask for the charter, I really don't know what's going on!" Later, a letter written to Mr. Hu Huaichen was found in his schoolbag. (Prepared to put in the mailbox) The police thought it was necessary to inquire, so they sent many detectives, accompanying him to Mr. Hu's house on Fulili Road, scaring Teacher Hu, who was living in peace and quiet in his humble home! Especially the family members. Later, after Mr. Hu proved his character and resume to the police, they all withdrew from Hu's house and took him back to the police station. The authorities warned him: "You have to be careful in the future, now go!" A false alarm ended here.

Haphazard Talks on Huanhua 203

Once a complete melon is torn into pieces, the glutton can fulfill his ambition of chewing it. Once a whole nation is disintegrated, foreigners will have the opportunity to nibble and devour it. Ice cream can relieve the summer heat, but it can also cause disease. Foreign insults can serve as a wake-up call to the dream of the sick man of East Asia, but they can also cause the sick man of East Asia to die without a burial place.

Mosquitoes and bedbugs use their poisonous hands when people are unprepared, and the victim's temporary resistance cannot match prevention.

Iced water can cool down the five-minute passion on people's bodies.

Hatred of goods can cool down the five-minute passion in people's hearts.

What is called heat? In the dictionary of adults and gentlemen, there is only the heat of being keen on fame and wealth. In the dictionary of ordinary people, there is the heat of being in deep water and scorching fire.

When people are in an unbearable and unspeakable situation, the proud sunlight is showing a victorious smile. Ah! Sun! Detestable! But you must know that victory is not permanent.

The methods that sunlight is now applying to us are only cruel and painful. Those who usually are pro-Japanese and flattering to Japan, you should wake up.

Living in a drunken dream and dying in a dream

Extremely Important Rural Hygiene – Yi Ping 204

It is said that this year's weather is the hottest in eight years. One of my classmates suggested going to the countryside for a few days, but the countryside is also just as hot. However, the flavor of the oxcart shed keeps people's minds from decaying. Originally, there were people who wrote special books discussing the city and the countryside. The content also focused on the flavor of the oxcart shed, but did not pay attention to rural hygiene. Although we only stayed for three days, we noticed a very tragic thing, or rather, it is the philosophy of the countryside.

On the second day of arriving in the countryside, a police officer and a doctor in uniform came. They went door to door to persuade people to get vaccinations, talking all day long about how terrible cholera is in the hot summer, especially after this year's war, the epidemic is even worse. We were sent by X County to give vaccinations and do not charge a fee, but no matter how hard you try to persuade them, the farmers are as afraid of getting vaccinated as if they were in a lawsuit, and they all shake their heads and run away.

We two had already received the first vaccination in Shanghai, so we asked them to give us the second vaccination. The farmers whispered to each other, as if getting vaccinated was a terrible thing. The police officer and the doctor smiled and said to us, "It's good to go back and report the results." After the police officer and the doctor left, they all gathered around to warn us.

"They are Japanese in disguise!" An old lady said this.

Of course, we gave them speeches, telling them that they should pay the most attention to hygiene in summer, and even said what was taught in elementary school (do not drink unclean water, do not eat raw and cold food), etc.

"Those who have studied in foreign schools all believe in foreign methods. Before there were Western doctors, didn't Chinese people still live? We country people all drink cold water from the river and sleep in oxcart sheds at night, and we don't hear of people dying every day. Doctors can give vaccinations, but can doctors themselves not die?" A healthy but not beautiful farmer yelled with gestures as if scolding someone.

We can't blame them for their words. In their eyes, their reasons are sufficient. Therefore, rather than saying that they don't pay attention to hygiene, it is better to say that it is because education in China is not widespread. If everyone could have four or six years of compulsory education, they would know what getting vaccinations and other things are all about.

The request is not approved. This instruction. ▲ Wang Wang Shi sues Wang Yanchang for abandonment. The man is strong and capable of supporting himself and does not have an abandonment problem. Notify him immediately. This instruction. ▲ Yu Zaiyou and others sue Wang Bingrong for contraband. Since it has been clearly ascertained by the investigators, it should be handed over to the Public Security Bureau for legal processing. Notify them immediately. This instruction. ▲ Xu Zhang Shi appeals and requests a review of the case file. The appeal should be submitted to the Nantong Court for review. The request to transfer the case file is not approved. Notify them immediately. This instruction. ▲ Shi Chunheng submits a filing statement. There is no explicit provision in the current Criminal Procedure Law for filing a case. The request should not be considered. This instruction.
